<p><i><b>Loud</b></i> is the fifth <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Studio_album" title="Studio album">studio album</a> by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barbadian_people" title="Barbadian people">Barbadian</a> singer <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>. It was released on November 12, 2010, by <a href="/wiki/Def_Jam_Recordings" title="Def Jam Recordings">Def Jam Recordings</a> and SRP Records. It was recorded between February and August 2010, during the singer's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Last_Girl_on_Earth_Tour" title="Last Girl on Earth Tour">Last Girl on Earth Tour</a> and the filming of her first feature film <i><a href="/wiki/Battleship_(film)" title="Battleship (film)">Battleship</a></i>. Rihanna was the executive producer of <i>Loud</i> and worked with various record producers, including <a href="/wiki/Stargate_(production_team)" title="Stargate (production team)">StarGate</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sandy_Vee" title="Sandy Vee">Sandy Vee</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Runners" title="The Runners">The Runners</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tricky_Stewart" title="Tricky Stewart">Tricky Stewart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alex_da_Kid" title="Alex da Kid">Alex da Kid</a>. The record features several guest vocalists, including rappers <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drake_(rapper)" title="Drake (rapper)">Drake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, who is featured on the sequel to "<a href="/wiki/Love_the_Way_You_Lie" title="Love the Way You Lie">Love the Way You Lie</a>", titled "<a href="/wiki/Love_the_Way_You_Lie_(Part_II)" title="Love the Way You Lie (Part II)">Love the Way You Lie (Part II)</a>".</p>
<p>The album differs from Rihanna's 2009 album, <i><a href="/wiki/Rated_R_(Rihanna_album)" title="Rated R (Rihanna album)">Rated R</a></i>, which incorporates a prominently foreboding and angry tone and dark themes. <i>Loud</i> features <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Up-tempo" title="Up-tempo">up-tempo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> genres, ranging from <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a> to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Electro_music" title="Electro music">electro</a> music, and marks the return to <a href="/wiki/Dancehall" title="Dancehall">dancehall</a>; a genre prominent on Rihanna's first two albums <i><a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Sun" title="Music of the Sun">Music of the Sun</a></i> (2005) and <i><a href="/wiki/A_Girl_like_Me_(Rihanna_album)" title="A Girl like Me (Rihanna album)">A Girl like Me</a></i> (2006). It also incorporates <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a> in "<a href="/wiki/California_King_Bed" title="California King Bed">California King Bed</a>" and <a href="/wiki/Reggae" title="Reggae">reggae</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> inspired "<a href="/wiki/Man_Down_(song)" title="Man Down (song)">Man Down</a>".</p>
<p><i>Loud</i> received generally positive reviews from music critics, who complimented its upbeat material and Rihanna's vocal performances, while others stated that although the songs were solid, they were unfocused to each other. The album was a commercial success internationally; it debuted at number three on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart, with first week sales of 207,000 copies, the highest first week sales of her career at the time. The album entered the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Albums_Chart" title="Canadian Albums Chart">Canadian</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Swiss_Albums_Chart" title="Swiss Albums Chart">Swiss</a> and <a href="/wiki/UK_Albums_Chart" title="UK Albums Chart">UK</a> album charts at number one. Since its release, it had sold over 8 million copies worldwide.</p>
<p>The album produced seven singles, including the international hits "<a href="/wiki/Only_Girl_(In_the_World)" title="Only Girl (In the World)">Only Girl (In the World)</a>", "<a href="/wiki/What%27s_My_Name%3F_(Rihanna_song)" title="What's My Name? (Rihanna song)">What's My Name?</a>", and "<a href="/wiki/S%26M_(song)" title="S&amp;M (song)">S&amp;M</a>". All three singles reached number one on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a>. "S&amp;M" was Rihanna's tenth number one song in the US, making Rihanna the youngest recording artist to accumulate the plateau in the shortest time, surpassing <a href="/wiki/Mariah_Carey" title="Mariah Carey">Mariah Carey</a>. "Only Girl (In the World)" won the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Dance_Recording" title="Grammy Award for Best Dance Recording">Grammy Award for Best Dance Recording</a> in February 2011; additionally, the album was nominated for three more Grammy Awards, including for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Album of the Year">Album of the Year</a>. To support the album, Rihanna embarked on her third worldwide concert tour, entitled the <a href="/wiki/Loud_Tour" title="Loud Tour">Loud Tour</a>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Background">Background</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Loud_(Rihanna_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Background">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Michael_Jackson1_1988.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="791" height="129" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Michael_Jackson1_1988.jpg/170px-Michael_Jackson1_1988.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Michael_Jackson1_1988.jpg/255px-Michael_Jackson1_1988.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/Michael_Jackson1_1988.jpg/340px-Michael_Jackson1_1988.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Michael_Jackson1_1988.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Vice_president" title="Vice president">vice president</a> of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Def_Jam" title="Def Jam">Def Jam</a>, Bu Thiam, compared the album with <a href="/wiki/Michael_Jackson" title="Michael Jackson">Michael Jackson</a>'s 1982 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bestseller_(music)" title="Bestseller (music)">bestseller</a> <i><a href="/wiki/Thriller_(Michael_Jackson_album)" title="Thriller (Michael Jackson album)">Thriller</a></i>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Following a domestic violence case between Rihanna and her boyfriend American entertainer <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chris_Brown_(American_entertainer)" title="Chris Brown (American entertainer)">Chris Brown</a>, media speculated as to whether any song featured on her fourth studio album would be about him.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-songbash_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-songbash-1">[1]</a></sup> The album was released in November 2009, under the title <i><a href="/wiki/Rated_R_(Rihanna_album)" title="Rated R (Rihanna album)">Rated R</a></i>. Primarily a <a href="/wiki/Pop_music" title="Pop music">pop</a> and <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> album,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wood_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wood-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-McCormick_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-McCormick-3">[3]</a></sup> it also incorporates musical elements of <a href="/wiki/Hip_hop_music" title="Hip hop music">hip hop</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">rock</a>, and dancehall.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenblatt_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-Greenblatt-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Powers_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-Powers-5">[5]</a></sup> <i>Rated R</i> was commercially successful and spawned five singles, including the international hit, "<a href="/wiki/Rude_Boy_(Rihanna_song)" title="Rude Boy (Rihanna song)">Rude Boy</a>". Six months after releasing the record, Rihanna began planning a fifth studio album, promising that her new material would be "more energetic" than her previous works.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Stargate_(production_team)" title="Stargate (production team)">StarGate</a>'s Tor Erik Hermansen, said "Rihanna came to us before we started recording "<a href="/wiki/Only_Girl_(In_the_World)" title="Only Girl (In the World)">Only Girl (In the World)</a>" and said ‘I feel great about myself. I want to go back to having fun, I want to make happy and up-tempo records'."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sean_Garrett" title="Sean Garrett">Sean Garrett</a> compared the sound of the new tracks with her previous hit singles "<a href="/wiki/Umbrella_(song)" title="Umbrella (song)">Umbrella</a>" and "Rude Boy".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_album_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-New_album-8">[8]</a></sup> In an interview for <a href="/wiki/MTV_(UK_and_Ireland)" title="MTV (UK and Ireland)">MTV UK</a>, the vice president of Def Jam Recordings compared the upcoming Rihanna album with Michael Jackson's <i><a href="/wiki/Thriller_(Michael_Jackson_album)" title="Thriller (Michael Jackson album)">Thriller</a></i> saying, "Rihanna is coming along incredibly. I’m trying to push her to where every song will be a hit from one to 12. I’m talking about NO album fillers. Our bar for this album is Michael Jackson's ‘Thriller’."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-New_album_8-1"><a href="#cite_note-New_album-8">[8]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recording_and_title">Recording and title</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Loud_(Rihanna_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Recording and title">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="quotebox" style="float: right; clear: right; margin: 0.5em 0 0.8em 1.4em; width:20%; padding: 6px; border: 1px solid #aaa; font-size: 88%; background-color: #F9F9F9;">
<div class="" style="position: relative; text-align: left;">
<div>
<p>"I'm done recording the whole album. I made sure not to let you down with my music! You guys are always defending me, so now you've got some great songs to justify it. I didn't want to go backward and remake [2007's] <a href="/wiki/Good_Girl_Gone_Bad" title="Good Girl Gone Bad">Good Girl Gone Bad</a>. I wanted the next step in the evolution of Rihanna, and it's perfect for us."</p>
</div>
</div>
<cite style="display: block; text-align: left;">—Rihanna talking about the concept of <i>Loud</i> for Rihannadaily.com<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Title_Reveal_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-Title_Reveal-9">[9]</a></sup></cite></div>
<p>Rihanna and <a href="/wiki/L.A._Reid" title="L.A. Reid">Antonio "L.A." Reid</a> assembled a group of songwriters and record producers at several recording studios in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> for two weeks to write songs for Rihanna; they wrote approximately 200 songs, eleven of which were included on the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RollingStone4_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-RollingStone4-10">[10]</a></sup> Def Jam rented out nearly every recording studio in Los Angeles in order to create as many songs as possible.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hiphopdx_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-hiphopdx-11">[11]</a></sup> Ray Daniels, the manager of musical duo <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock_City_(musical_duo)" title="Rock City (musical duo)">Rock City</a> (brothers Theron and Timothy Thomas), was present during the sessions, and stated that a writing camp typically involves the label hiring ten recording studios for two weeks at the cost of $25,000 per day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRP_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-NRP-12">[12]</a></sup> Daniels revealed that it is where songwriters have lyrics but no music, and where producers have music but no lyrics.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NRP_12-1"><a href="#cite_note-NRP-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<p>Singer-songwriters and producers <a href="/wiki/Taio_Cruz" title="Taio Cruz">Taio Cruz</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alex_da_Kid" title="Alex da Kid">Alex da Kid</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Sean_Garrett" title="Sean Garrett">Sean Garrett</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ne-Yo" title="Ne-Yo">Ne-Yo</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rico_Love" title="Rico Love">Rico Love</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rap-up1_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-rap-up1-17">[17]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Timbaland" title="Timbaland">Timbaland</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rap-up1_17-1"><a href="#cite_note-rap-up1-17">[17]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Shontelle" title="Shontelle">Shontelle</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/David_Guetta" title="David Guetta">David Guetta</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drake_(entertainer)" title="Drake (entertainer)">Drake</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> contributed to the album. "<a href="/wiki/DJ_Got_Us_Fallin%27_in_Love" title="DJ Got Us Fallin' in Love">DJ Got Us Fallin' in Love</a>" was written for Rihanna, but the song was rejected and was subsequently sent to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)" title="Usher (entertainer)">Usher</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RollingStone4_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-RollingStone4-10">[10]</a></sup> With regard to "<a href="/wiki/What%27s_My_Name%3F_(Rihanna_song)" title="What's My Name? (Rihanna song)">What's My Name?</a>", Rihanna thought Drake could understand the melody of the song and invited him to work on the track when she played him the finishbozed recording.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> The collaboration was originally planned to be a remix, but later it was decided that the version featuring Drake would be used as the original.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Loud</i> was recorded in various recording studios worldwide including the Larrabee Sound Studios, <a href="/wiki/The_Village_(studio)" title="The Village (studio)">The Village</a> and <a href="/wiki/Westlake_Recording_Studios" title="Westlake Recording Studios">Westlake Recording Studios</a> in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a>, Platinum Sound Recording Studios, and Roc the Mic Studios in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> and The Bunker Studios in <a href="/wiki/Paris" title="Paris">Paris</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> In September 2010, during a webchat with her fansite Rihannadaily.com, Rihanna announced that the album would be called <i>Loud</i>, saying "get Loud everybody, get crazy, get excited, because I'm pumped. I'm just gonna be me, because that's what you guys love the most, and that's what makes me feel best. Just being normal, normal for me is Loud! Sassy, fun, flirty, energetic."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Title_Reveal_9-1"><a href="#cite_note-Title_Reveal-9">[9]</a></sup> While Rihanna was filming <i>Battleship</i>, she explained in an interview with <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Tonight" title="Entertainment Tonight">Entertainment Tonight</a></i>, "Loud is, the word, the name of the album definitely reflects the attitude of it, it's really sassy and flirty and it grabs your attention and that's why I enjoy it. It takes you through a really really interesting ride. So colorful the album."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Composition">Composition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Loud_(Rihanna_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Composition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Influence_and_sound">Influence and sound</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Loud_(Rihanna_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Influence and sound">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Loud</i> is a departure from the personal, melodramatic themes of <i>Rated R</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cinquemani_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cinquemani-25">[25]</a></sup> Stylistically, it is a return to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Caribbean_music" title="Caribbean music">Caribbean</a>-inspired dance-pop of Rihanna's earlier work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Conner_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-Conner-26">[26]</a></sup> Ryan Burleson of <a href="/wiki/Consequence_of_Sound" title="Consequence of Sound">Consequence of Sound</a> described the album as "a dynamic <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a> record".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Burleson_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-Burleson-27">[27]</a></sup> In an interview with <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>, Rihanna said "I wanted songs that were all Rihanna songs, that nobody else could do. I didn't want the generic pop record that <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ke$ha" title="Ke$ha">Ke$ha</a> or <a href="/wiki/Lady_Gaga" title="Lady Gaga">Lady Gaga</a> or <a href="/wiki/Katy_Perry" title="Katy Perry">Katy Perry</a> could just do and it'll work. I wanted a song, or songs, that were Rihanna songs, that only I could do, had that little <a href="/wiki/West_Indian" title="West Indian">West Indian</a> vibe to it, had that certain tone, a certain sass and a certain energy."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> During the promotion of <i>Loud</i>, Rihanna said that much of the music was born out of frustration. She explained: "When you go to a club and have to listen to bad music you revert to the liquor, because you want to have a good time. I hate having to skip a track. I wanted to make an album you can just play."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-S.26M_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-S.26M-29">[29]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Songs">Songs</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Loud_(Rihanna_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Songs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="mbox-small-left" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;float:left">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><img alt="" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></div>
</div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em">
<div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Rihanna_-_Only_Girl_(In_the_World).ogg" title="File:Rihanna - Only Girl (In the World).ogg">"Only Girl (In the World)"</a></div>
<div>
<div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio class="kskin" controls="" data-durationhint="23.253333333333" data-mwprovider="local" data-mwtitle="Rihanna_-_Only_Girl_(In_the_World).ogg" data-startoffset="0" id="mwe_player_0" preload="none" style="width:220px">

</div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">"Only Girl (In the World)" features a "heavy whipping bass" with the chorus of the song incorporating a "strobing, dance club beat", which also been described as a "stronger, sexier version" of her 2007 single, "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Stop_the_Music_(Rihanna_song)" title="Don't Stop the Music (Rihanna song)">Don't Stop the Music</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AOL1_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-AOL1-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MME_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-MME-31">[31]</a></sup></div>
</div>
<hr/>
<div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Rihanna_-_S%26M.ogg" title="File:Rihanna - S&amp;M.ogg">"S&amp;M"</a></div>
<div>
<div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio class="kskin" controls="" data-durationhint="20.51" data-mwprovider="local" data-mwtitle="Rihanna_-_S&amp;M.ogg" data-startoffset="0" id="mwe_player_1" preload="none" style="width:220px">
<source data-bandwidth="52081" data-height="0" data-shorttitle="Ogg source" data-title="Original Ogg file (52 kbps)" data-width="0" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/b3/Rihanna_-_S%26M.ogg" type='audio/ogg; codecs="vorbis"'></source>
<track data-dir="ltr" data-mwprovider="local" data-mwtitle="TimedText:Rihanna_-_S&amp;M.ogg.en.srt" kind="subtitles" label="English (en) subtitles" src="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=TimedText:Rihanna_-_S%26M.ogg.en.srt&amp;action=raw&amp;ctype=text%2Fx-srt" srclang="en" type="text/x-srt"></track></audio></div>
</div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">S&amp;M's lyrics have been noted by some critics as being "R-rated", although some critics considered "S&amp;M" to be one of the better <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a> songs from <i>Loud</i>, as it efficiently balanced "Rihanna's playful and sinister sides".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup></div>
</div>
<hr/></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing these files? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>The opening track "S&amp;M" is an up-tempo <a href="/wiki/Eurodance" title="Eurodance">eurodance</a> song<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> produced by Norwegian producers StarGate and Sandy Vee. The song is reminiscent of <a href="/wiki/Depeche_Mode" title="Depeche Mode">Depeche Mode</a>'s 1984 song "<a href="/wiki/Master_and_Servant" title="Master and Servant">Master and Servant</a>"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolk_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Wolk-34">[34]</a></sup> and contains lyrical thoughts of <a href="/wiki/Sadomasochism" title="Sadomasochism">sadomasochism</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wolk_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-Wolk-34">[34]</a></sup> Andy Kellman of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allmusic" title="Allmusic">Allmusic</a> regarded "S&amp;M" as a <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a> song which efficiently balanced "Rihanna's playful and sinister sides".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kellman_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kellman-35">[35]</a></sup> "What's My Name?" was also produced by StarGate and features guest vocals from <a href="/wiki/Canadians" title="Canadians">Canadian</a> rapper <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drake_(entertainer)" title="Drake (entertainer)">Drake</a>. It is a mid-tempo, <a href="/wiki/Electronic_music" title="Electronic music">electro</a>-<a href="/wiki/Contemporary_R%26B" title="Contemporary R&amp;B">R&amp;B</a> song with a back track consisting of heavy reggae. The song also sees Rihanna's return to the "Island-pop" style of her early career".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Cheers_(Drink_to_That)" title="Cheers (Drink to That)">Cheers (Drink to That)</a>" is a pop rock song produced by <a href="/wiki/The_Runners" title="The Runners">The Runners</a>, and interpolates <a href="/wiki/Avril_Lavigne" title="Avril Lavigne">Avril Lavigne</a>'s 2002 single "<a href="/wiki/I%27m_with_You_(song)" title="I'm with You (song)">I'm with You</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> Mark Savage from <a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">BBC News</a> described the song as a funky, loping guitar groove for a night out on the town.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Savage_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Savage-40">[40]</a></sup> "Only Girl (In the World)" was the third song from the album produced by StarGate. It is an up-tempo <a href="/wiki/Dance-pop" title="Dance-pop">dance-pop</a> song that incorporates elements of <a href="/wiki/Eurodance" title="Eurodance">eurodance</a> in its production.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AOL1_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-AOL1-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MME_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-MME-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Brad Wete, a reviewer of <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i>, described Rihanna's vocals as "seductive" and reminiscent of a "stronger, sexier version" of her 2007 single, "<a href="/wiki/Don%27t_Stop_the_Music_(Rihanna_song)" title="Don't Stop the Music (Rihanna song)">Don't Stop the Music</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MME_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-MME-31">[31]</a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/California_King_Bed" title="California King Bed">California King Bed</a>" is a rock <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Power_ballad" title="Power ballad">power ballad</a>; Ryan Dombell of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Media" title="Pitchfork Media">Pitchfork Media</a> compared it to the <a href="/wiki/Aerosmith" title="Aerosmith">Aerosmith</a> song, "<a href="/wiki/I_Don%27t_Want_to_Miss_a_Thing" title="I Don't Want to Miss a Thing">I Don't Want to Miss a Thing</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> The <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Shama_Joseph&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Shama Joseph (page does not exist)">Shama Joseph</a> produced "<a href="/wiki/Man_Down_(song)" title="Man Down (song)">Man Down</a>" is a reggae song with an electro rhythm, in which Rihanna sings in a West Indian accent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pareles_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pareles-46">[46]</a></sup> "<a href="/wiki/Raining_Men_(Rihanna_song)" title="Raining Men (Rihanna song)">Raining Men</a>" is a hip-hop song, which features rap vocals from Trinidadian rapper <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a>. Rihanna described the song as a fun song that differs from the original, referring to the 1979 single by <a href="/wiki/The_Weather_Girls" title="The Weather Girls">The Weather Girls</a> with similar title "<a href="/wiki/It%27s_Raining_Men" title="It's Raining Men">It's Raining Men</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raining_Men_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-Raining_Men-47">[47]</a></sup> "Complicated" was produced by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Christopher_Stewart_(music_producer)" title="Christopher Stewart (music producer)">Tricky Stewart</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ester_Dean" title="Ester Dean">Ester Dean</a>. Leah Greenblatt from <i>Entertainment Weekly</i> said "Even while telling a recalcitrant man how hard he is to love, she [Rihanna] sounds almost buoyant, her newly expanded vocals eager to scale the song's high-altitude house beat".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Greenblatt_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-Greenblatt-4">[4]</a></sup> The final track is the <a href="/wiki/Sequel" title="Sequel">sequel</a> to Rihanna's <a href="/wiki/Duet" title="Duet">duet</a> with <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Love_the_Way_You_Lie" title="Love the Way You Lie">Love the Way You Lie</a>". "<a href="/wiki/Love_the_Way_You_Lie_(Part_II)" title="Love the Way You Lie (Part II)">Love the Way You Lie (Part II)</a>", which was produced by <a href="/wiki/Alex_da_Kid" title="Alex da Kid">Alex da Kid</a>, features Rihanna as the protagonist and lead vocalist, viewing aspects of a relationship from a female perspective, unlike the original, which featured Eminem as lead vocalist and was from a male perspective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Singles">Singles</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Loud_(Rihanna_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Singles">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<table class="mbox-small-left" role="presentation" style="border:1px solid #aaa;background-color:#f9f9f9;float:left">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div class="center">
<div class="floatnone"><img alt="" data-file-height="160" data-file-width="160" height="50" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/50px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/75px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></div>
</div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text plainlist" style="line-height:1.1em">
<div class="haudio">
<div style="padding:4px 0"><a href="/wiki/File:Rihanna_-_What%27s_My_Name_(Feat._Drake).ogg" title="File:Rihanna - What's My Name (Feat. Drake).ogg">"What's My Name?"</a></div>
<div>
<div class="mediaContainer" style="width:220px"><audio class="kskin" controls="" data-durationhint="25.982244897959" data-mwprovider="local" data-mwtitle="Rihanna_-_What's_My_Name_(Feat._Drake).ogg" data-startoffset="0" id="mwe_player_2" preload="none" style="width:220px">

</div>
<div class="description" style="padding:2px 0 0 0">The album's second single, which features guest vocals by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drake_(entertainer)" title="Drake (entertainer)">Drake</a>, features an "island-pop" style and a backing track with "heavy reggae". Critics praised Rihanna's vocal performance in the song, as well as the romantic nature and its sexual tones.</div>
</div>
<hr/></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td class="mbox-text" colspan="2" style="line-height:1.1em"><span><i>Problems playing this file? See <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Media_help" title="Wikipedia:Media help">media help</a>.</i></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>"<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Only_Girl_(in_the_World)" title="Only Girl (in the World)">Only Girl (In the World)</a>" was released as the album's lead single on September 10, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> The song was sent to US <a href="/wiki/Contemporary_hit_radio" title="Contemporary hit radio">mainstream</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rhythmic_contemporary" title="Rhythmic contemporary">rhythmic</a> radio on September 21, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mainstream_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Mainstream-50">[50]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rhythmic_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rhythmic-51">[51]</a></sup> It received positive reviews from music critics, who praised its chorus and thunderous dance beats.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> The song reached number one on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_Hot_100" title="Billboard Hot 100"><i>Billboard</i> Hot 100</a> chart, in the UK, Canada, Australia, Austria, Belgium (Wallonia), Ireland, Israel, Italy, New Zealand, Norway and Slovakia, becoming one of her best charting songs to date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> At the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/53rd_Grammy_Awards" title="53rd Grammy Awards">53rd Grammy Awards</a>, held at the <a href="/wiki/Staples_Center" title="Staples Center">Staples Center</a> in <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles" title="Los Angeles">Los Angeles</a> on February 13, 2011, "Only Girl (In the World)" won the award for <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Dance_Recording" title="Grammy Award for Best Dance Recording">Best Dance Recording</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tribune_Company_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tribune_Company-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Drake_at_Bun-B_Concert_2011.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1224" data-file-width="999" height="208" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Drake_at_Bun-B_Concert_2011.jpg/170px-Drake_at_Bun-B_Concert_2011.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Drake_at_Bun-B_Concert_2011.jpg/255px-Drake_at_Bun-B_Concert_2011.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Drake_at_Bun-B_Concert_2011.jpg/340px-Drake_at_Bun-B_Concert_2011.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Drake_at_Bun-B_Concert_2011.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Canadian rapper <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drake_(rapper)" title="Drake (rapper)">Drake</a> provided vocals on "What's My Name?"</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/What%27s_My_Name%3F_(Rihanna_song)" title="What's My Name? (Rihanna song)">What's My Name?</a>", which features guest vocals by Canadian recording artist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drake_(rapper)" title="Drake (rapper)">Drake</a>, was released as the album's second single; it was sent to US mainstream and rhythmic radios on September 21, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Music critics praised the song as some of Rihanna's best vocal work to date, noting the romantic nature of the song and its sexual tones. The song peaked at number one on the US <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 chart, giving Rihanna her eighth number-one on the chart,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboard-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-billboard2_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-billboard2-58">[58]</a></sup> while "Only Girl (In the World)" became her ninth number-one song two weeks after "What's My Name?".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> It reached number one in the United Kingdom and became Rihanna's fifth UK number one single and Drake's first.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>The collaboration with <a href="/wiki/Nicki_Minaj" title="Nicki Minaj">Nicki Minaj</a>, "<a href="/wiki/Raining_Men_(Rihanna_song)" title="Raining Men (Rihanna song)">Raining Men</a>", was sent to <a href="/wiki/Urban_contemporary" title="Urban contemporary">urban</a> radio on December 7, 2010 as an urban radio single and third track from <i>Loud</i> as a single in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Raining_Men_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-Raining_Men-47">[47]</a></sup> It peaked at number 48 on the US <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%26B/Hip-Hop_Songs" title="R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs"><i>Billboard</i> R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Songs</a> chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> "Raining Men" received mixed reviews from critics who praised the chemistry between Rihanna and Minaj but criticised the song for failing to create anything new or original.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kellman_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-Kellman-35">[35]</a></sup> "S&amp;M", the album's fourth US single and third international single, was solicited to US mainstream radio on January 25, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-allaccess.com_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-allaccess.com-63">[63]</a></sup> Reception of "S&amp;M" was mixed; some reviewers criticized the overt use of sexual lyrics while others noted it as a stand-out track from <i>Loud</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sun_Times_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sun_Times-64">[64]</a></sup> A remix of the song which features guest vocals by <a href="/wiki/Britney_Spears" title="Britney Spears">Britney Spears</a>, was digitally released on April 11, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup> "S&amp;M" reached the top ten in twenty-four countries and peaked at number one in Australia, Canada and the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>"<a href="/wiki/Man_Down_(song)" title="Man Down (song)">Man Down</a>" was released as the fifth international single in some European countries in July 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-FRANCE_68-0"><a href="#cite_note-FRANCE-68">[68]</a></sup> It received positive reviews from critics, who called it a return to Rihanna's Caribbean-tinged rhythm. "Man Down" reached a peak of 59 on the US <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100 chart. In France, it peaked at number one for five consecutive weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> "California King Bed" was released as the fourth international single on May 13, 2011,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup> and as the sixth US single. It was sent to US <a href="/wiki/Adult_contemporary_music" title="Adult contemporary music">Hot/Modern adult contemporary radio</a> on May 16, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AllAccessHotAC_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-AllAccessHotAC-71">[71]</a></sup> The song peaked at number four in Australia and New Zealand<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> and number eight on the <a href="/wiki/UK_Singles_Chart" title="UK Singles Chart">UK Singles Chart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> On July 24, 2011, Rihanna announced the release of "Cheers (Drink to That)" as the seventh single from the album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The single was released to US mainstream and rhythmic radio on August 2, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cheers_Radio_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cheers_Radio-76">[76]</a></sup> The song peaked at number seven on the US <i>Billboard</i> Hot 100,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US.2F.7CUSPop.2FUS_Radio.7CCanadian_peak_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-US.2F.7CUSPop.2FUS_Radio.7CCanadian_peak-77">[77]</a></sup> and number twelve on the US <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mainstream_Top_40_(Pop_Songs)" title="Mainstream Top 40 (Pop Songs)">Pop Songs</a> chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US.2F.7CUSPop.2FUS_Radio.7CCanadian_peak_77-1"><a href="#cite_note-US.2F.7CUSPop.2FUS_Radio.7CCanadian_peak-77">[77]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release_and_promotion">Release and promotion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Loud_(Rihanna_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Release and promotion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Loud</i> was released on November 12, 2010, in four separate editions: a standard edition; a deluxe edition, packaged in a <a href="/wiki/Digipak" title="Digipak">digipak</a> exclusively for the US and Australia, that features a 30-minute documentary <i>Making of Loud</i> DVD (Directed by Brian and Brad Palmer); a Couture Edition containing the deluxe edition of <i>Loud</i> with a deluxe cover art lithograph, a box set with enhanced clear couture cover and a full-size photo book.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> An Ultra Couture Edition was also produced, containing a copy of the Deluxe Edition of <i>Loud</i> signed by <a href="/wiki/Rihanna" title="Rihanna">Rihanna</a>, the MP3 download of <i>Loud</i> on <a href="/wiki/Street_date" title="Street date">street date</a> and all the features of the Couture Edition. The Ultra Couture Edition sold out and is no longer available neither on Amazon or her online store.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> An explicit version of <i>Loud</i> was also released and features a <a href="/wiki/Parental_Advisory" title="Parental Advisory">Parental Advisory</a> label due to some of the lyrical content.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The Japanese edition of the album was released with two additional remixes of "Only Girl (In the World)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> The piano version of "Love the Way You Lie (Part II)" was only available with the <a href="/wiki/ITunes" title="ITunes">iTunes</a> edition of the album. However, the version which features <a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Eminem</a> was available for purchase.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Live_performances">Live performances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Loud_(Rihanna_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Live performances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rihanna,_LOUD_Tour,_Oakland_4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="640" height="188" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Rihanna%2C_LOUD_Tour%2C_Oakland_4.jpg/250px-Rihanna%2C_LOUD_Tour%2C_Oakland_4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Rihanna%2C_LOUD_Tour%2C_Oakland_4.jpg/375px-Rihanna%2C_LOUD_Tour%2C_Oakland_4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Rihanna%2C_LOUD_Tour%2C_Oakland_4.jpg/500px-Rihanna%2C_LOUD_Tour%2C_Oakland_4.jpg 2x" width="250"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rihanna,_LOUD_Tour,_Oakland_4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rihanna performing "Only Girl (In the World)" on the Loud Tour.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Rihanna embarked on a promotional tour across Europe and North America to promote the album's release. The singer performed "Only Girl (In the World)", the lead single, live for the first time in North America on <i><a href="/wiki/Saturday_Night_Live" title="Saturday Night Live">Saturday Night Live</a></i> on October 30, 2010, and debuted the second single, "What's My Name?", later on in the show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> The following day in the United Kingdom, Rihanna sang "Only Girl (In the World)" on <a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK_series_7)" title="The X Factor (UK series 7)">series seven</a> of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK)" title="The X Factor (UK)">The X Factor</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> Rihanna performed "Only Girl (In the World)" at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MTV_Europe_Music_Awards_2010" title="MTV Europe Music Awards 2010">MTV Europe Music Awards 2010</a> in Madrid, Spain, on November 7, 2010,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> on <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/X_Factor_(Italy)" title="X Factor (Italy)">The X Factor</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a> on November 9, 2010,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> and on <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Grand_Journal_(Canal%2B)" title="Le Grand Journal (Canal+)">Le Grand Journal</a></i> in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> on November 10, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> On November 11, 2010, Rihanna appeared on a pre-recorded edition of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Graham_Norton_Show" title="The Graham Norton Show">The Graham Norton Show</a></i> in the United Kingdom, where she gave an interview and sang "Only Girl (In the World)".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> On November 15, before the album's US release, Rihanna reprised her performance of "What's My Name?" for <a href="/wiki/MTV" title="MTV">MTV</a>'s <i>The Seven</i>, live from <a href="/wiki/Times_Square" title="Times Square">Times Square</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> The next day, Rihanna performed "What's My Name?" on the <i><a href="/wiki/Late_Show_with_David_Letterman" title="Late Show with David Letterman">Late Show with David Letterman</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> On November 17, 2010, Rihanna was interviewed and performed "Only Girl (In the World)" and "What's My Name?" on <i><a href="/wiki/Good_Morning_America" title="Good Morning America">Good Morning America</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> Rihanna performed a medley of "Love the Way You Lie (Part II)", "What's My Name?" and "Only Girl (In the World)" at the <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards_of_2010" title="American Music Awards of 2010">American Music Awards of 2010</a> on November 21, 2010, where she won the award for <a href="/wiki/American_Music_Award_for_Favorite_Soul/R%26B_Female_Artist" title="American Music Award for Favorite Soul/R&amp;B Female Artist">Favorite Soul/R&amp;B Female Artist</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-AMA2010_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-AMA2010-93">[93]</a></sup> Rihanna opened with an a cappella version of "Love The Way You Lie Part II".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup></p>
<p>On December 11, 2010, Rihanna returned to <a href="/wiki/The_X_Factor_(UK_series_7)" title="The X Factor (UK series 7)">series seven</a> of the UK's <i>The X Factor</i>, to perform "<a href="/wiki/Unfaithful_(song)" title="Unfaithful (song)">Unfaithful</a>" with finalist <a href="/wiki/Matt_Cardle" title="Matt Cardle">Matt Cardle</a>, as well as a solo of "What's My Name?".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> The finale was watched by fifteen million viewers; however, the episode generated thousands of complaints about Rihanna's choice of outfit and sexual performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> Rihanna performed the song with Drake for the first time at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/53rd_Grammy_Awards" title="53rd Grammy Awards">53rd Grammy Awards</a> on February 13, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> Rihanna also appeared at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/2011_BRIT_Awards" title="2011 BRIT Awards">2011 BRIT Awards</a> on February 15, 2011, where she performed "S&amp;M" for the first time, as a medley with "Only Girl (In the World)" and "What's My Name?".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> Rihanna was requested to "tone down" her performance of "S&amp;M" by the show's producers, and she performed only one verse and chorus in between "Only Girl (In The World)" and "What's My Name?". The BRIT Awards corporation wanted to avoid receiving complaints similar to those received by the <i>X-Factor</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Rihanna was a special guest at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NBA_All_Star_Game" title="NBA All Star Game">NBA All Star Game</a> on February 20, 2011, where she performed a medley of "<a href="/wiki/Umbrella_(song)" title="Umbrella (song)">Umbrella</a>", "Only Girl (In the World)", "<a href="/wiki/Rude_Boy_(Rihanna_song)" title="Rude Boy (Rihanna song)">Rude Boy</a>", "What's My Name?" (with Drake) and "<a href="/wiki/All_of_the_Lights" title="All of the Lights">All of the Lights</a>" (with <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup></p>
<p>Rihanna performed "California King Bed" in the style of a <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">country music</a> song for the first time with <a href="/wiki/Sugarland" title="Sugarland">Sugarland</a> front woman <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Nettles" title="Jennifer Nettles">Jennifer Nettles</a>, during the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ACM_Awards" title="ACM Awards">ACM Awards</a> held by the <a href="/wiki/Academy_of_Country_Music" title="Academy of Country Music">Academy of Country Music</a> on April 3, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> She was a guest on the <a href="/wiki/American_Idol_(season_10)" title="American Idol (season 10)">tenth season</a> of the US series <i><a href="/wiki/American_Idol" title="American Idol">American Idol</a></i> on April 14, 2011, where she performed "California King Bed".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup> Rihanna promoted "California King Bed" with performances in Milan, Paris and Hamburg, because she was appointed ambassador for <a href="/wiki/Nivea" title="Nivea">Nivea</a> skincare.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> Rihanna opened the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Billboard_Music_Awards" title="Billboard Music Awards"><i>Billboard</i> Music Awards</a> on May 22, 2011, performing the remix of "S&amp;M" with Britney Spears at the <a href="/wiki/MGM_Grand_Garden_Arena" title="MGM Grand Garden Arena">MGM Grand Garden Arena</a> in Las Vegas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup> The performance attracted complaints about the overt sexual nature of the broadcast on a publicly owned television channel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup> Rihanna performed on <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>'s <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Today_(NBC_program)" title="Today (NBC program)">Today</a></i> show on May 27, 2011 as part of a Summer Concert Series. She performed "S&amp;M", "Only Girl (In the World)", "What's My Name?" and "California King Bed".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tour">Tour</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Loud_(Rihanna_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Tour">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Loud_Tour" title="Loud Tour">Loud Tour</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Rihanna,_LOUD_Tour,_Florida_8.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Rihanna%2C_LOUD_Tour%2C_Florida_8.jpg/220px-Rihanna%2C_LOUD_Tour%2C_Florida_8.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Rihanna%2C_LOUD_Tour%2C_Florida_8.jpg/330px-Rihanna%2C_LOUD_Tour%2C_Florida_8.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d6/Rihanna%2C_LOUD_Tour%2C_Florida_8.jpg/440px-Rihanna%2C_LOUD_Tour%2C_Florida_8.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Rihanna,_LOUD_Tour,_Florida_8.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rihanna performing "What's My Name?" on the Loud Tour.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>To further promote <i>Loud</i>, Rihanna embarked on her fourth concert tour, the Loud Tour, in June 2011, having announced it on February 9, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> The tour comprised 101 show dates, 32 in North America, 1 in Central America, 4 in South America and 64 in Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pollstar_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-pollstar-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup> Tickets sold well in the United Kingdom and some additional shows were added. She performed ten shows at London's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_O2_Arena_(London)" title="The O2 Arena (London)">O<sub>2</sub> Arena</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Rihanna was interviewed by <a href="/wiki/Ryan_Seacrest" title="Ryan Seacrest">Ryan Seacrest</a> on <i>American Idol</i>, and talked about the design of the stage, stating: "We've just designed the stage and we have a section that we are building ... where the fans can actually be in the show and in the stage and be closer than they've ever been. It's real VIP."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup> The North American leg of the tour began on June 4, 2011 in <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>, <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup> Originally, <a href="/wiki/J._Cole" title="J. Cole">J. Cole</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cee_Lo_Green" title="Cee Lo Green">Cee Lo Green</a> were planned as supporting acts for the North American leg. However, Green left the tour, citing schedule conflicts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> Rappers <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Drake_(entertainer)" title="Drake (entertainer)">Drake</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kanye_West" title="Kanye West">Kanye West</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jay-Z" title="Jay-Z">Jay-Z</a> made guest appearances on some dates to perform their collaborations "What's My Name?", "<a href="/wiki/Run_This_Town" title="Run This Town">Run This Town</a>", "All of the Lights" and "Umbrella", respectively.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-117"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> The tour was received positively by critics, with some calling it "Rihanna's best tour yet". Jane Stevenson of the <i><a href="/wiki/Toronto_Sun" title="Toronto Sun">Toronto Sun</a></i> commented that "the two-hour, larger-than-life show lived up to the billing."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup> Jon Brean of the Minneapolis "<a href="/wiki/Star_Tribune" title="Star Tribune">Star Tribune</a>" remarked, "The Barbadian singer is more visually and vocally dynamic than she has ever been before."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup></p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>

1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/49/Star_empty.svg/22px-Star_empty.svg.png 2x" width="11"/></span><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cinquemani_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cinquemani-25">[25]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle"><i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i></td>
<td style="text-align:center;vertical-align:middle">8/10<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anderson_126-0"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson-126">[126]</a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><i>Loud</i> received generally positive reviews from <a href="/wiki/Music_journalism" title="Music journalism">music critics</a>. At <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, which assigns a <a href="/wiki/Standard_score" title="Standard score">normalized</a> rating out of 100 given to reviews from mainstream critics, the album received an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weighted_mean" title="Weighted mean">average</a> score of 67, based on 22 reviews.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jon_Pareles" title="Jon Pareles">Jon Pareles</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> perceived a "hermetic, cool calculation" on the album, writing that it "works the pop gizmos as neatly as any album this year, maintaining the Rihanna brand".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pareles_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pareles-46">[46]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Leah Greenblatt commented that <i>Loud</i> shows Rihanna "undefeated by her worst circumstances — and finding redemption in exactly the kind of pop nirvana that made her famous in the first place".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated2_128-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated2-128">[128]</a></sup> James Reed of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boston_Globe" title="The Boston Globe">The Boston Globe</a></i> called the album "an unabashed return to where Rihanna belongs: the dance floor" and stated: "As if liberating herself from the depths, she's a force on these 11 songs".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Reed_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-Reed-129">[129]</a></sup> Stacey Anderson of <i><a href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)" title="Spin (magazine)">Spin</a></i> commended Rihanna's "full, healthy claim to her sexuality" and wrote that the album "offers a confident female ethos on par with the best of <a href="/wiki/Shakira" title="Shakira">Shakira</a> or <a href="/wiki/Beyonc%C3%A9" title="Beyoncé">Beyoncé</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Anderson_126-1"><a href="#cite_note-Anderson-126">[126]</a></sup></p>
<p>Genevieve Koski of <i><a href="/wiki/The_A.V._Club" title="The A.V. Club">The A.V. Club</a></i> commended Rihanna for elevating the album's generic sound, writing that she "does sound invigorated, delivering charismatic vocal performances of material that doesn’t always warrant them".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Koski_120-1"><a href="#cite_note-Koski-120">[120]</a></sup> Emily Mackay of <i><a href="/wiki/NME" title="NME">NME</a></i> felt that its "experiments feel more organic, its tone better paced" than <i>Rated R</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mackay_123-1"><a href="#cite_note-Mackay-123">[123]</a></sup> Thomas Conner of the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Sun-Times" title="Chicago Sun-Times">Chicago Sun-Times</a></i> wrote that "the celebratory atmosphere of Rihanna's sassy new jams are seasoned with some of the darker flavors from <span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span><i>Rated R</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Conner_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-Conner-26">[26]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pitchfork_Media" title="Pitchfork Media">Pitchfork Media</a>'s Ryan Dombal complimented the album's "effervescent pop" and stated: "Her laissez-faire attitude toward hit-making on <i>Loud</i> can result in too-safe moves or semi-experiments that come off surprisingly great".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dombal_124-1"><a href="#cite_note-Dombal-124">[124]</a></sup> Ed Power of <i><a href="/wiki/Hot_Press" title="Hot Press">Hot Press</a></i> complimented its "unabashedly subtext-free" songs and found its hooks "way beyond addictive."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup></p>
<p>In a mixed review, Andy Kellman of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Allmusic" title="Allmusic">Allmusic</a> found the album's material "slapdash" and "uneven", and called it "more an unfocused assortment of poor-to-solid songs than a unified set".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kellman_35-3"><a href="#cite_note-Kellman-35">[35]</a></sup> Andy Gill of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> felt that "the more interesting tracks are those with less salacious demands on her vulnerability".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Gill_121-1"><a href="#cite_note-Gill-121">[121]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Slant_Magazine" title="Slant Magazine">Slant Magazine</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s Sal Cinquemani commended that "the subtle West Indian flavor with which Rihanna and company have smartly imbued" most of the album, although he noted some flaws in its production and wrote that "Rihanna has always had trouble fitting into one genre ... and for better or worse, Rihanna continues to stylistically branch out on <i>Loud</i>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cinquemani_25-2"><a href="#cite_note-Cinquemani-25">[25]</a></sup> Hugh Montgomery of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Observer" title="The Observer">The Observer</a></i> commented that "sonically, it's fairly unremarkable ... but its strident buoyancy is difficult to resist".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Montgomery_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-Montgomery-131">[131]</a></sup></p>
<p>"Only Girl (in the World)" won the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Dance_Recording" title="Grammy Award for Best Dance Recording">Grammy Award for Best Dance Recording</a> at the <a href="/wiki/53rd_Annual_Grammy_Awards" title="53rd Annual Grammy Awards">53rd Annual Grammy Awards</a> and the album was nominated for three awards at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/54th_Grammy_Awards" title="54th Grammy Awards">54th Grammy Awards</a>, including <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Album_of_the_Year" title="Grammy Award for Album of the Year">Album of the Year</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Pop_Vocal_Album" title="Grammy Award for Best Pop Vocal Album">Best Pop Vocal Album</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rap/Sung_Collaboration" title="Grammy Award for Best Rap/Sung Collaboration">Best Rap/Sung Collaboration</a> for "What's My Name?".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Commercial_performance">Commercial performance</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Loud_(Rihanna_album)&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Commercial performance">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><i>Loud</i> debuted at number three on the US <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> chart, with first-week sales of 207,000 copies in the United States, giving Rihanna her highest first-week sales in the US at that time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> It also debuted at number one on <i><a href="/wiki/Billboard_charts" title="Billboard charts">Billboard</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">'</span>s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/R%26B/Hip-Hop_Albums" title="R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums">R&amp;B/Hip-Hop Albums</a> chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup> In its second week, the album dropped to number six on the <i>Billboard</i> 200 and sold 141,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup> By its thirteenth week, the album returned to its peak at number three and sold 62,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup> However, in its fourteenth week, the album dipped to number ten on the Billboard 200 with 45,000 copies sold.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> In its fifteenth week, <i>Loud</i> rose to number eight, selling an additional 33,000 copies in the US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup> By July 3, 2011, <i>Loud</i> was the eleventh-best selling album of 2011 in the United States, selling 598,000 copies between January 1, 2011 and July 3, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> On January 25, 2011, <i>Loud</i> was certified platinum in the United States, denoting shipments of over one million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RIAA_140-0"><a href="#cite_note-RIAA-140">[140]</a></sup> <i>Loud</i> ranked as <i>Billboard</i> magazine's ninth-most successful album of 2011 on their year-end charts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> As of June 2015, the album has sold 1.8 million copies in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-US_Album_Sales_142-0"><a href="#cite_note-US_Album_Sales-142">[142]</a></sup></p>
<p><i>Loud</i> was also a commercial success outside of the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-dutch_143-0"><a href="#cite_note-dutch-143">[143]</a></sup> In Canada, it debuted at number one on the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Albums_Chart" title="Canadian Albums Chart">Canadian Albums Chart</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> selling 27,000 copies in its first week.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> <i>Loud</i> sold more than 80,000 units in Canada, achieving platinum status by the first week of December 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Canadian_Platinum_Certification_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-Canadian_Platinum_Certification-146">[146]</a></sup> By September 8, 2011, <i>Loud</i> had sold more than 240,000 copies in Canada.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CRIA_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-CRIA-147">[147]</a></sup> In France, the album debuted at number three with first-week sales of 17,304 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ChartsFrance_148-0"><a href="#cite_note-ChartsFrance-148">[148]</a></sup> By its sixth week on the French charts, <i>Loud</i> achieved platinum status, reaching the 100,000 copies mark.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SNEP_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-SNEP-149">[149]</a></sup> In France, the album has sold 355,000 copies as of April 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> In its second week on the Australian Albums Chart, <i>Loud</i> was certified platinum for shipments of over 70,000 copies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> In Italy, the album reached number eleven.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ITA_152-0"><a href="#cite_note-ITA-152">[152]</a></sup> It became Rihanna's highest charting album there until her sixth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Talk_That_Talk" title="Talk That Talk">Talk That Talk</a></i> (2011) surpassed the record. <i>Loud</i> was her third consecutive number-one album in Switzerland.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SWI_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-SWI-153">[153]</a></sup> <i>Loud</i> debuted at number two on the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_Albums_Chart" title="German Albums Chart">German Albums Chart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup></p>
<p>The album debuted at number two in the United Kingdom, with first week sales of 91,000 units.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> In its fifth week, the album sold 306,107 copies in the United Kingdom, giving the singer her first platinum-selling week in her career.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> In its seventh week on the chart, <i>Loud</i> reached number one, giving Rihanna her second UK number-one album. After seven weeks of sales, the album became the fourth best-selling album of 2010 in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> The album had sold 1,800,000 copies in the United Kingdom by September 4, 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-UK_New_Sales_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-UK_New_Sales-158">[158]</a></sup> By December 16, 2011, <i>Loud</i> was certified six-times platinum by the <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a> (BPI), marking shipments of 1.8 million copies to retailers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BPI_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-BPI-159">[159]</a></sup> It was the biggest selling R&amp;B album of 2011 in the UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> As of August 2012, <i>Loud</i> is the fifth biggest selling digital album of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> As of March 2015, <i>Loud</i> is the 45th best-selling album of the millennium in the United Kingdom.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> As of November 2011, the album has sold over 8 million copies worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wwsales_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-wwsales-163">[163]</a></sup></p>
